<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer7455767619751995624">A huge, mysterious iron man stands at the top of a cliff, surveying the ocean. His eyes glow white, red, infrared. Then, he lifts one enormous foot and steps out into nothingness. Crraaasssssh! His head, arms, legs, ears, hands all break off as he tumbles onto the rocks below. The end of the story? No, it's only the beginning of this modern parable of peace in the universe</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7455767619751995624">A huge, mysterious iron man stands at the top of a cliff, surveying the ocean. His eyes glow white, red, infrared. Then, he lifts one enormous foot and steps out into nothingness. Crraaasssssh! His head, arms, legs, ears, hands all break off as he tumbles onto the rocks below. The end of the story? No, it's only the beginning of this modern parable of peace in the universe. The Iron Giant has an insatiable appetite for barbed wire, tractors, and rusty chains. While farmers and townspeople run around trying to stop him, destroy him, capture him, only one boy understands what must be done. Meanwhile, an even bigger threat hovers over the land, in the shape of an evil-looking space-bat-angel-dragon. How will the people of the world survive the impending doom?<p> Ted Hughes, poet laureate of England, first wrote this compelling tall tale in 1968. Clearly, the need for its message of peace has not diminished in the decades since. Simple, repetitive sentences carry the mesmerizing spirit of traditional fairy tales. And Andrew Davidson's black-and-white illustrations, with their menacing air and timeless appeal, drive the point home in vivid style. (Ages 8 and older) <em>--Emilie Coulter</em></p></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7455767619751995624">...more</a>

      <a href="/user/show/922495-patrick" class="user" title="Patrick">Patrick</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1142817636">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12008336920766820964">When you write a review of a kid's book, there really should be a way to give it two different star ratings. One for you, and one for the kids you've read it to. <br /><br />For me, this book might be a three star book. Four if I was feeling generous. I find it wordy and ponderous. Overwrought. The plot is pretty clunky and meh. I don't hate the book or anything, it's just doesn't do much for me. <br /><br />But my boy loves it. He wants me to read it to him over and over again. And again. <br /><br />I think this might be slightl</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12008336920766820964">When you write a review of a kid's book, there really should be a way to give it two different star ratings. One for you, and one for the kids you've read it to. <br /><br />For me, this book might be a three star book. Four if I was feeling generous. I find it wordy and ponderous. Overwrought. The plot is pretty clunky and meh. I don't hate the book or anything, it's just doesn't do much for me. <br /><br />But my boy loves it. He wants me to read it to him over and over again. And again. <br /><br />I think this might be slightly because my boy loves the movie The Iron Giant a lot. But that can't be too much of the reason, as the book has only a glancing similarity to the movie.<br /><br />(The movie is A+ excellent, by the way. One of my favorite movies ever.)</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_666418184">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/666418184" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10478000-april" class="left imgcol" title="April"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1439652786p2/10478000.jpg" alt="April" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/666418184?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 13, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10478000-april" class="user" title="April">April</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/119502.The_Iron_Man" title="Paperback 9780571226122" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to April by: </span>
      Kirsty
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=childrens" class="actionLinkLite">childrens</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=sci-fi" class="actionLinkLite">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=favourites" class="actionLinkLite">favourites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=short-story-or-stories" class="actionLinkLite">short-story-or-stories</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=loved" class="actionLinkLite">loved</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=read-in-2013" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer666418184">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4157357398597807391">(Read for book club - 13/07/2013)<br /><blockquote>“Haven’t you heard of the music of the spheres?” asked the dragon. “It’s the music that space makes to itself. All the spirits inside all the stars are singing. I’m a star spirit. I sing too. The music of the spheres is what makes space so peaceful.”</blockquote> <br /><br />I suppose the only way I could start this review would be by saying that approximately thirteen years ago a small, likely annoying girl of four's heart was torn apart by the ending scene of Brad Bird's <em>The Iron Giant</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4157357398597807391">(Read for book club - 13/07/2013)<br /><blockquote>“Haven’t you heard of the music of the spheres?” asked the dragon. “It’s the music that space makes to itself. All the spirits inside all the stars are singing. I’m a star spirit. I sing too. The music of the spheres is what makes space so peaceful.”</blockquote> <br /><br />I suppose the only way I could start this review would be by saying that approximately thirteen years ago a small, likely annoying girl of four's heart was torn apart by the ending scene of Brad Bird's <em>The Iron Giant.</em> Never before has the phrase 'You are who you choose to be' and the robotic 'Superman' evoked such a pitiful flurry of tears in that of a hard-faced infant who, as I'm rightfully reminded of by my Dad, refused to see another film for months afterwards due to the sheer trauma (and, ironically, missed the concluding scene because she was too upset to continue watching it). <br /><br />Seeing as though <em>The Iron Giant</em> is quite possibly one of my favourite films in the whole world, it was to be expected that I'd experience some powerful waves of nostalgia as I sifted through Hughes' work. I wasn't wrong! If I’ve learnt anything about these things, it’s that learning the origins of something so emotionally embalmed in one's life can be either disastrous or wonderful, and I'm pleased to say it was the latter that I felt about <em>The Iron Man</em> as a whole. Charmingly illustrated, beautifully told and captivating in its own way, I loved every page. It shares the delicacy conveyed in the beginning scene, when we find the Iron Giant about to topple down the cliff into the sea, wrapped in the silence of the world. I never gave Hughes much of a chance given his relation to another writer who – I'm positive other GR users will no doubt agree –I'm very fond of, but I'm thoroughly enthused to read more of his work after finishing this. I was toying with giving this a five star rating but declined merely because it wasn't blown away territory and I'm generally quite picky about awarding a book the full amount of stars. Still, it misses only by an inch, as it really is lovely. <br /><br />A rusty fairy tale of sorts; remarkable in vision, gorgeous in words. A new favourite.<br /><br />Also: everyone go see the movie. Go, go, go!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4157357398597807391">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1265329001">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1265329001" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11245979-suad-shamma" class="left imgcol" title="Suad Shamma"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1449167883p2/11245979.jpg" alt="Suad Shamma" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1265329001?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 03, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11245979-suad-shamma" class="user" title="Suad Shamma">Suad Shamma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/119502.The_Iron_Man" title="Paperback 9780571226122" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11245979-suad-shamma?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11245979-suad-shamma?shelf=2015" class="actionLinkLite">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1265329001">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5858705522465690523">I was thrilled when I got this copy of The Iron Man from my husband. I've always loved the movie The Iron Giant, and have it almost memorized in its entirety! I never knew that it was based on a book, nor that it was a book written by Ted Hughes! <br /><br />I shamefully admit that this was my first Ted Hughes book, and although I enjoyed it, it was close to nothing like the movie. That put me off for many reasons, but the biggest being that I was reading it with the movie playing in my head, which was prob</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5858705522465690523">I was thrilled when I got this copy of The Iron Man from my husband. I've always loved the movie The Iron Giant, and have it almost memorized in its entirety! I never knew that it was based on a book, nor that it was a book written by Ted Hughes! <br /><br />I shamefully admit that this was my first Ted Hughes book, and although I enjoyed it, it was close to nothing like the movie. That put me off for many reasons, but the biggest being that I was reading it with the movie playing in my head, which was probably my mistake. <br /><br />The Iron Man was more of a victim-turned-hero in this book than he was made to be in the movie, and the fighting scene at the end against the big black dragon from space was insanely brilliant. I thoroughly enjoyed it and the cleverness behind it.<br /><br />I would recommend to all who decide to read this book and have watched the film adaptation beforehand to think of it as completely independent from the movie. Otherwise, you will find yourself disappointed, as did I.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5858705522465690523">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1397023299">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1397023299" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/28547777-ian-laird" class="left imgcol" title="Ian Laird"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1395488526p2/28547777.jpg" alt="Ian Laird" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1397023299?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 02, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/28547777-ian-laird" class="user" title="Ian Laird">Ian Laird</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1369884.The_Iron_Man" title="Paperback 9780571136773" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/28547777-ian-laird?shelf=childrens" class="actionLinkLite">childrens</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/28547777-ian-laird?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/28547777-ian-laird?shelf=favourite-covers" class="actionLinkLite">favourite-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1397023299">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16205244072270557437">I suspect few come to this book without having first seen the film adaptation called <em>The Iron Giant</em>, the 1999 Warner Brothers animation directed by Brad Bird and co-written by him.<br /><br />The film is a masterpiece and is also one of my *favourite films, to watch again and again whenever it comes on. The book is wonderful but perhaps not a masterpiece. Let us deal first with the book, because I think it is necessary and pleasurable to return to the film.<br /><br />The charm of the book stems from the central idea o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16205244072270557437">I suspect few come to this book without having first seen the film adaptation called <em>The Iron Giant</em>, the 1999 Warner Brothers animation directed by Brad Bird and co-written by him.<br /><br />The film is a masterpiece and is also one of my *favourite films, to watch again and again whenever it comes on. The book is wonderful but perhaps not a masterpiece. Let us deal first with the book, because I think it is necessary and pleasurable to return to the film.<br /><br />The charm of the book stems from the central idea of the impact caused by the arrival on Earth of a giant mechanical man. He can deconstruct then reconstruct himself by way of his component parts being handily equipped with homing devices so that they can link up with each other. Simply, the metal man falls down a cliff into the sea, the local famers relax until he returns and starts eating their tractors, so they build a big pit to trap him. When the giant falls in they fill it with earth. Before too long the metal man resurfaces, and is befriended by a small boy called Hogarth, who comes up with the idea of accommodating the visitor’s special needs by putting him in a scrap metal yard. When a space dragon comes to Earth (Australia, wouldn’t you know it), the iron man devises a challenge to outwit the monster and turn him from foe to the beneficiary of all the peoples of the Earth. <br /><br />The story is in five parts. Or to give the story its proper subtitle: <strong>A Children’s Story in Five Nights</strong>. This is the other important element of the charm of <strong>The Iron Man</strong>. The story reads like it is being told to wide-eyed children, sitting enthralled. A child as we know does not always require complete logic and the story of a big metal man from space is a gripping one. So is his developing friendship with Hogarth. The whole dragon sequence is, of course, fantastic in the literal sense but also, very appealing to small children. <br /><br />While remaining true to the spirit of the book, the animated film <em>The Iron Giant</em> improves the story by giving it a better narrative arc and locating the tale very specifically in a 1950s cold war environment, when the organs of authority (government, security agencies, the army) were perhaps more respected than they are now, certainly powerful, but nevertheless susceptible to paranoia and suspicion. A big metal machine is just the thing to disturb their shaky equilibrium. The threat to the iron giant does not come externally but arises from the paranoia of the time - where does the creature come from? Is it made by the Russians? The Chinese? It represents an unknown danger: it must be destroyed. <br /><br />This is in stark contrast to Hogarth’s thinking and those close to him. Hogarth understands the nature of the giant and that he is friendly: their relationship is wonderful, witness doing water bombs into the forest pool. In the film Hogarth, has a single mother and he is befriended by the beatnik sculptor who runs the scrap yard, both uncomfortable types in the 1950s. The sculptor in particular with his art, coffee and penchant for jazz represents a disturbing anti-establishment perspective. The soundtrack is superb too. <br /><br />In this way the story remains integrated and coherent, while maintaining faith with the source material: the ultimate threat comes from the sky, but this time is of their own making. Read the book and see the film!<br /><br />*To provide some context, current favourites include: <em>Pleasantville</em>, <em>Blast from the Past</em>, <em>Cars</em> and Ben Stiller’s remake of <em> The Secret Life of Walter Mitty</em>.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16205244072270557437">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_321997820">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/321997820" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5951384-catherine-mcdonald" class="left imgcol" title="Catherine McDonald"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Catherine McDonald" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/321997820?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 01, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5951384-catherine-mcdonald" class="user" title="Catherine McDonald">Catherine McDonald</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/119502.The_Iron_Man" title="Paperback 9780571226122" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer321997820">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9520999226813501819">The Iron Man by Ted Hughes<br />The Iron Man: A Children’s Story In Five nights by Ted Hughes does indeed consist of five chapters; designed to be read a chapter per day, although some children may find it difficult to wait a whole day to hear more of this exciting story.<br />Set in a rural town, a town where a small boy called Hogarth goes fishing in the local stream only to come across an Iron Man. He forms a relationship with the Iron Man and he must save him from the adults. The fact that when he does</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9520999226813501819">The Iron Man by Ted Hughes<br />The Iron Man: A Children’s Story In Five nights by Ted Hughes does indeed consist of five chapters; designed to be read a chapter per day, although some children may find it difficult to wait a whole day to hear more of this exciting story.<br />Set in a rural town, a town where a small boy called Hogarth goes fishing in the local stream only to come across an Iron Man. He forms a relationship with the Iron Man and he must save him from the adults. The fact that when he does tell the grown-ups that they believe him and are unsure what to do really makes this story thrilling for children as they realise they are on an even footing with the adults. It is Hogarth that helps when the adults wants to trap it and when the Earth is in it’s hour of need; prey to an enormous bat-angel creature from space that threatens to devour every living thing on the planet, it is again Hogarth, the child, that sees the only one that can help is the Iron Man. Children love this book as it has adventure, mystery and explores different relationships.<br />I think it is an excellent book to use as a stimulus in science or to create cross curricular links when reading it in literacy.<br />You can look at the properties of different materials. What might have happened if the ‘Iron Man’ was made of wood, plastic, fabric or jelly? Plan an experiment to test the strength of different materials. A lot of silhouette illustrations are used in the book so you can cross over with light and shadows in science and get the children to make their own shadow robot puppets. <br />For ICT you could make a stop motion animation based on the story. <br />The book is also an excellent basis for looking at harmony within the world and how peace is created. The Iron Man wants to bring peace to the world and so possibly in Year 6, you can look at what war does and how to create peace in the world. It could be the basis in a debate possibly for PHSE or even a philosophy lesson where the answer may not be possible to find. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9520999226813501819">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_345933417">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/345933417" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6154879-rhian-loxley" class="left imgcol" title="Rhian Loxley"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1315161789p2/6154879.jpg" alt="Rhian Loxley" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/345933417?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 10, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6154879-rhian-loxley" class="user" title="Rhian Loxley">Rhian Loxley</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/119502.The_Iron_Man" title="Paperback 9780571226122" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer345933417">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10181994350044409158">I am about to start reading the Iron man with my year three class, and I cannot wait. <br /><br />Having had the pleasure and vivid memories of being read this story by one of my own teachers when I was at school. I was a little apprehensive as to whether I would enjoy reading this book again, now that i am an adult. I need not have worried, Ted Hughes' writing is magical and this story was made to be read aloud. In fact I have enjoyed reading it so much, that over the half term holiday I read the story alo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10181994350044409158">I am about to start reading the Iron man with my year three class, and I cannot wait. <br /><br />Having had the pleasure and vivid memories of being read this story by one of my own teachers when I was at school. I was a little apprehensive as to whether I would enjoy reading this book again, now that i am an adult. I need not have worried, Ted Hughes' writing is magical and this story was made to be read aloud. In fact I have enjoyed reading it so much, that over the half term holiday I read the story aloud to my partner on a long car journey to Wales. The suspense and the visual imagery that builds as you read, really is spectacular.<br /><br />Having done my research, I am now aware of how Hughes came to write the Iron Man and it did not surprise me that the Iron Man was a story that Hughes made up over the course of five nights of storytelling to his children. After every part of the story he would go to his study and write it up just as he had told it. With this in mind it makes complete sense that the story reads aloud with such great ease and expression.<br /><br />From this story I will be doing a series of 3 lessons this week. My first lesson will be about forming opinions based upon the theme of recycling. On Tuesday we will be building character portraits, based upon the first chapter we will observe how our visualisations of the Iron Man progress as the story unfolds. Wednesday will see us doing a picture the author activity where we find out about Ted Hughes and make links between our knowledge of how and why he wrote the story and his use of pace and language. Next week we will be looking at character empathy and comparing characters from different stories as we are currently reading the BFG as our shared reading book.<br /><br />I would recommend this story as both a great book for reading for pleasure and also as a book to base a series of lessons on.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10181994350044409158">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/365267353" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10839357-sarfraz" class="left imgcol" title="Sarfraz"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Sarfraz" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/365267353?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 10, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10839357-sarfraz" class="user" title="Sarfraz">Sarfraz</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/119502.The_Iron_Man" title="Paperback 9780571226122" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer365267353">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5555077182954102988">The Iron Man book is one of the most remembered books from my childhood.<br /><br />The adventure starts with an immediate introduction of the Iron Man, giving great detail in his appearance. The suspense quickly builds up as the Iron Man falls down the cliff and in to little pieces. The body parts then start to reassemble, one by one until the Iron Man is complete. A little boy named Hogarth appears on the scene, fishing in a stream before he is startled by the Iron Man. Hogarth runs home to raise the alar</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5555077182954102988">The Iron Man book is one of the most remembered books from my childhood.<br /><br />The adventure starts with an immediate introduction of the Iron Man, giving great detail in his appearance. The suspense quickly builds up as the Iron Man falls down the cliff and in to little pieces. The body parts then start to reassemble, one by one until the Iron Man is complete. A little boy named Hogarth appears on the scene, fishing in a stream before he is startled by the Iron Man. Hogarth runs home to raise the alarm and with the help of the adults, the Iron Man is buried alive. But when danger approaches and the Earth is threatened, it is the Iron Man who comes to the humans aid.<br /><br />The Iron Man, from the beginning, intrigues the imagination of children with statements like "how far had he walked?" and "where did he come from?” It gets them to start thinking before an adult even asks them a question. The vocabulary is simple yet effective with an informative writing style. The book can be read to a class; it can therefore be enjoyed by children of all ages whether they are 5 years old or 9. It is very effective for holding children's attention, even more so if an adult decides to verbally add some special effects along with hand/body gestures in sync with what is happening in the story.<br /><br />The Iron Man can lead on to further related activities depending on the age group of the children, for example: younger children could be asked to draw what they think the Iron Man looks like, others could be asked to construct their very own Iron Man using materials and elder children could use the simple 5 chapter structure of the Iron Man to form their very own adventures.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5555077182954102988">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_498599113">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/498599113" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10813578-gareth-roberts" class="left imgcol" title="Gareth Roberts"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Gareth Roberts" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/498599113?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 07, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10813578-gareth-roberts" class="user" title="Gareth Roberts">Gareth Roberts</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/119502.The_Iron_Man" title="Paperback 9780571226122" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer498599113">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer195533095384562815">The Iron Man by Ted Hughes is a book that I came across due to the year four class I was placed in using the book for the basis of their Autumn terms literacy lessons. The Iron Man is a third person account of a metal eating iron giant who falls from space to impact on Hogarth's and the rest of the village's lives. <br /> The book was used successfully as the basis for a combination of literacy lessons due to the authors use of many literary devices which the class were required to learn that term. It</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText195533095384562815">The Iron Man by Ted Hughes is a book that I came across due to the year four class I was placed in using the book for the basis of their Autumn terms literacy lessons. The Iron Man is a third person account of a metal eating iron giant who falls from space to impact on Hogarth's and the rest of the village's lives. <br />	The book was used successfully as the basis for a combination of literacy lessons due to the authors use of many literary devices which the class were required to learn that term. It allowed the children to see how using devices such as metaphors, similes, climax and onomatopoeia could be used in their writing to make it more interesting to the reader. As well its use as being an example of creative writing, the Iron Man was used to teach other forms of writing such as newspaper reports, letter writing and persuasive argument. As the Iron Man is a short novel, the children were able to unpick the various themes within the book. The chapters are relatively short and all end with a climax, making the reader want to read on and the children begging for more. <br />	I would recommend all primary teachers read the Iron Man as it can be very useful in the classroom. It is suitable for KS1 and KS2 with different themes having greater relevance for difference age groups. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="195533095384562815">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1751772672282195368">I bought this book based purely on how much I loved Brad Bird's movie adaptation, <u>The Iron Giant</u>. And I think the excellence of the film completely overshadowed this book in my readings.<br /><br />Hughes has a simple, lyrical style that works for younger readers. And he divides the chapters into episodes to make it easily digestible. However, the story itself has no real depth of character, and prefers to stay detached in describing the realm of the fantastic. We never really see Hogarth and the Giant beco</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1751772672282195368">I bought this book based purely on how much I loved Brad Bird's movie adaptation, <u>The Iron Giant</u>. And I think the excellence of the film completely overshadowed this book in my readings.<br /><br />Hughes has a simple, lyrical style that works for younger readers. And he divides the chapters into episodes to make it easily digestible. However, the story itself has no real depth of character, and prefers to stay detached in describing the realm of the fantastic. We never really see Hogarth and the Giant become friends. And the appearance of the space dragon is an interesting trickster fairytale spin, but it doesn't fit organically with the previous episodes of the Iron Giant on Earth. If I hadn't watched the movie I would probably be more forgiving, because the story has its charms. But when compared to the animated classic, <em>The Iron Giant</em> seems smaller in comparison.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2833706886530861490">A 1001 CBYMRBYGU. One day, an Iron Giant arrives on earth. He eats barbed wire and tractors and plows, causing problems for the farmers. Finally, the farmers devise a trap for the Iron Giant and they successfully capture him. Then an even more terrible creature arrives from space and the Iron Giant must come to the rescue.<br /><br />“The peoples of the world got together. If they fed it, how could they ever satisfy it? It would never be full, and every new day it would be as hungry as ever. How can you feed a beast the size of Australia? Australia is a vast land, all the countries of Europe will fit easily into Australia. The monster’s stomach alone must be the size of Germany. No, they would not feed it.”<br /><br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1328898766">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1328898766" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5721271-matti-karjalainen" class="left imgcol" title="Matti Karjalainen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1311618462p2/5721271.jpg" alt="Matti Karjalainen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1328898766?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5721271-matti-karjalainen" class="user" title="Matti Karjalainen">Matti Karjalainen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/24173969-rautamies" title="Hardcover 9518732671" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5721271-matti-karjalainen?shelf=fantasia" class="actionLinkLite">fantasia</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5721271-matti-karjalainen?shelf=scifi" class="actionLinkLite">scifi</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5721271-matti-karjalainen?shelf=1940-1969" class="actionLinkLite">1940-1969</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5721271-matti-karjalainen?shelf=brittil%C3%A4inen-kauno" class="actionLinkLite">brittiläinen-kauno</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5721271-matti-karjalainen?shelf=romaanit" class="actionLinkLite">romaanit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5721271-matti-karjalainen?shelf=mieskirjailijat" class="actionLinkLite">mieskirjailijat</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5721271-matti-karjalainen?shelf=viitos-kuutoset" class="actionLinkLite">viitos-kuutoset</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1328898766">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14281547610084969120">Vuonna 1968 ilmestynyt Ted Hughesin "Rautamies" (Kustannus-Mäkelä, 1993) on klassikon aseman saavuttanut englantilainen lastenkirja, joka on tullut tutuksi myös The Whon <a title="Pete Townshend" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/282494.Pete_Townshend"> Pete Townshend</a>in rock-oopperana ja Brad Birdin animaatioelokuvana. Meillä se ei ole ehkä saavuttanut samanlaista mainetta ja kuuluisuutta, mistä kertonee sekin, että kirjan ensimmäinen ja ainoa painos otettiin vuonna 1993.<br /><br />Tarina käynnistyy väkevästi. Valtavan kokoinen Rautamies nousee merestä ja ryhtyy syömään metallia. Olennon</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14281547610084969120">Vuonna 1968 ilmestynyt Ted Hughesin "Rautamies" (Kustannus-Mäkelä, 1993) on klassikon aseman saavuttanut englantilainen lastenkirja, joka on tullut tutuksi myös The Whon <a title="Pete Townshend" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/282494.Pete_Townshend"> Pete Townshend</a>in rock-oopperana ja Brad Birdin animaatioelokuvana. Meillä se ei ole ehkä saavuttanut samanlaista mainetta ja kuuluisuutta, mistä kertonee sekin, että kirjan ensimmäinen ja ainoa painos otettiin vuonna 1993.<br /><br />Tarina käynnistyy väkevästi. Valtavan kokoinen Rautamies nousee merestä ja ryhtyy syömään metallia. Olennon ruokahalu on sen verran massiivinen, että alas sen suusta menevät niin jyväjemmarien traktorit kuin muutkin maalaiskoneet. Harri-nimisen pojan avulla Rautajätti saadaan sitten aisoihin ja samalla sille keksitään mielekästä tekemistä.<br /><br />Mutta ei siinä vielä kaikki! Maapallolle saapuu mantereen kokoinen Avaruuslepakko, joka liiskaa alleen Australian ja vaatii että ihmisten on tuotava hänelle mitä tahansa syötävää, kunhan se on vaan elollista. Sotahan siitä seuraa, mutta pyssyt ja pommit eivät tehoa lepakkoon. Niinpä avuksi kutsutaan Rautamies, joka haastaa ja lopulta voittaa Avaruuslepakon. Loppu onkin sitten sen verran kosminen että oksat pois ja jazztupakka palamaan. <br /><br /><em>"Etkö ole kuullut äärettömyyden laulua?", kysyi avaruuslepakko. "Se on musiikkia, jota avaruus luo itselleen. Kaikki tähtien henget laulavat. Minäkin olen tähden henki."</em> <br /><br />Ja niin saavutetaan maailmanrauha ja yleinen harmonia, mistä kaikkien on kiittäminen juuri tuota nimenomaista äärettömyyden laulua. Groovy, baby... Sääli vaan, että australialaiset musertuivat.<br /><br />Tarina etenee vauhdikkaasti, itse asiassa niin kovaa kyytiä ettei minkäänlaista jännitettä pääse oikein syntymään, ja kaiken lisäksi henkilöhahmot jäävät harmillisen pintapuolisiksi.<br /><br />Suosittelisinko "Rautamiestä" vekaroille? En tiedä, voisin ehkä kokeilla kolmos-nelosiin, sillä todella helposti tästä rakentaisi toimivan vinkkauksen.<br /><br />Lopuksi kiinnostava kirjallinen pikkufakta: Ted Hughes oli naimisissa <a title="Sylvia Plath" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4379.Sylvia_Plath"> Sylvia Plath</a>in kanssa.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14281547610084969120">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_245129121">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/245129121" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6216690-sara-hannon" class="left imgcol" title="Sara Hannon"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1360963497p2/6216690.jpg" alt="Sara Hannon" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/245129121?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 09, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6216690-sara-hannon" class="user" title="Sara Hannon">Sara Hannon</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/724659.The_Iron_Giant" title="Paperback 9780375801532" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6216690-sara-hannon?shelf=science-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer245129121">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1774702224600961736">Contains Spoilers<br /><br />1. Science Fiction<br /><br />2. The Iron Giant tells the story of a giant made of iron, who after making peace with local farmers, manages to save the world from a giant space dragon. <br /><br />3. I actually loved this book up until the end. The beginning is great, where the kid feels guilty about what they do to the Iron Giant, and then when the space dragon arrives, the panic and response of Earth is realistic and interesting. Then it takes a turn that I thought was a cop-out. There is this great</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1774702224600961736">Contains Spoilers<br /><br />1. Science Fiction<br /><br />2. The Iron Giant tells the story of a giant made of iron, who after making peace with local farmers, manages to save the world from a giant space dragon. <br /><br />3. I actually loved this book up until the end. The beginning is great, where the kid feels guilty about what they do to the Iron Giant, and then when the space dragon arrives, the panic and response of Earth is realistic and interesting. Then it takes a turn that I thought was a cop-out. There is this great battle of strength and wits between the Iron Giant and the space dragon, which the Iron Giant barely wins. Then instead of the dragon being banished back into space and the Earth is saved, Hughes decides to make the dragon a "star spirit" and has him fly around the planet every night singing the song that makes space peaceful. It eventually makes the Earth peaceful. That is nice and everything, but the dragon's explanation for his act of evil in landing on Earth and demanding to be fed living things is absolutely illogical. He says it is because he just felt like it, he heard all the violence on Earth and decided he would land and join in by eating everyone on the planet. To me that makes no sense. It seems to me that there was this wonderfully creative story and then we had to figure out some way to make the ending world peace. <br /><br />4. This is a nice little story. Despite my hatred of the ending, it is a great "David and Goliath" story that shows that just because someone is bigger than you or looks scarier than you, that does not mean they are necessary mean or evil. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1774702224600961736">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_71800332">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71800332" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/223837-nikki" class="left imgcol" title="Nikki"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" alt="Nikki" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/71800332?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 19, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/223837-nikki" class="user" title="Nikki">Nikki</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1369884.The_Iron_Man" title="Paperback 9780571136773" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/223837-nikki?shelf=children-s-and-ya" class="actionLinkLite">children-s-and-ya</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/223837-nikki?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer71800332">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6473772593398159865">I remember this book as being magic. I know when I was quite young I had both this and The Iron Woman. I didn't like that as much. I'm doing a children's lit module this next semester, so I dug out a lot of "childhood classics" or books I adored as a kid to reread, or at least glance at. It doesn't take long to reread The Iron Man (or The Iron Giant, as my sister's copy insists).<br /><br />The back calls it a modern fairytale, which is true. It's purely fantastical, with a big iron man and a bit space-drag</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6473772593398159865">I remember this book as being magic. I know when I was quite young I had both this and The Iron Woman. I didn't like that as much. I'm doing a children's lit module this next semester, so I dug out a lot of "childhood classics" or books I adored as a kid to reread, or at least glance at. It doesn't take long to reread The Iron Man (or The Iron Giant, as my sister's copy insists).<br /><br />The back calls it a modern fairytale, which is true. It's purely fantastical, with a big iron man and a bit space-dragon-bat-thing. I liked the way it was told, but I think I also found it a little creepy when I was younger. Also, as an adult, the two halves of the story fit a little oddly -- in the first half, the Iron Man is silent and a menace. In the second half, he becomes this heroic clever figure. Maybe it's something you need to be a child to accept.<br /><br />The moral at the end is simple and nice enough, but kind of out of the blue.<br /><br />Still, I thought it was magic as a child and I'll give it the rating the child would have given it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6473772593398159865">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1367421700">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1367421700" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/44827714-baysal-hassan" class="left imgcol" title="Baysal Hassan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1439824168p2/44827714.jpg" alt="Baysal Hassan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1367421700?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 19, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/44827714-baysal-hassan" class="user" title="Baysal Hassan">Baysal Hassan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/119502.The_Iron_Man" title="Paperback 9780571226122" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1367421700">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer335545848899493863">‘The Iron Man’: A Children’s Story in Five Nights is made up of five chapters, the story was designed to be read to children over five nights but unfortunately I was unable to follow this routine and as a result the story was read in less than an hour. Each chapter ended with a climax, ‘how far had he walked? Nobody knows. Where had he come from nobody knows?’ and therefore I was drawn into the exciting and engaging story about the Iron Man. <br /><br />‘The Iron Man’ is a story about a mysterious ‘metal ma</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText335545848899493863">‘The Iron Man’: A Children’s Story in Five Nights is made up of five chapters, the story was designed to be read to children over five nights but unfortunately I was unable to follow this routine and as a result the story was read in less than an hour. Each chapter ended with a climax, ‘how far had he walked? Nobody knows. Where had he come from nobody knows?’ and therefore I was drawn into the exciting and engaging story about the Iron Man. <br /><br />‘The Iron Man’ is a story about a mysterious ‘metal man’ who suddenly appears out of the sea one night and after managing to fall of the cliff, in a peculiar way he assembles himself. The story is set in a rural town; within the town a small boy named Hogarth goes fishing one day and there he comes across an Iron Man. Hogarth and the Iron man become friends but there is an issue, the Iron Man loves to eat metal and this soon becomes a major problem for the local farmers, so a plan is made with the help of Hogarth.<br /><br />The story can be viewed as a modern fairy tale which embeds a mixture of fantasy and real life adventure. It contains many themes such as friendship, betrayal, loyalty, destruction and many more. <br /><br />In terms of ‘The Iron Man’ and its relevance to the classroom personally I believe that Ted Hughes novel is suitable for KS1 and KS2 children, ages ranging from 5 to 11. Depending on the age group the activities and tasks can be adapted to meet the children’s needs. <br /><br />The story is very imaginative and descriptive and consequently the story can be used to inspire children (KS2) in their creative writing. Hughes, uses many different language techniques within the story: metaphors, similes, onomatopoeia’s and climax. Within lessons students could be asked to identify the different language techniques used within the novel:for example, ‘how many similes/metaphors can you identify?’ and to make the task even more advanced the students could be asked to write their own simile/metaphor describing the Iron Man. Also, there are many other literacy tasks that students can be asked to produce for instance, re writing the first chapter from the Iron man’s point of view, taking into consideration the Iron man’s thoughts and feelings. <br /><br />Besides Literacy, Ted Hughes’ novel is versatile and can be used in many cross curricular activities for example it can be related to science/design and technology. In terms of DT the children could begin by redesigning the Iron man using different materials and then plan an experiment (science) to test the strength/properties of the materials used (wood, paper, plastic. There are many more cross curricular links possible – geography, ICT and PSHE. <br /><br />As an adult I very much enjoyed reading this story as it was very suspenseful and creative, so I can imagine how excited and thrilled children would be whilst reading and interacting with this novel.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="335545848899493863">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15383002499197046121">This story appears to be some sort of mythic allegory? Or something else. It may yet come to me. Maybe I should give it another star just for giving me something to puzzle about. The writing got smoother along the way as if the author were learning English, and yet Hughes, well, British poet and all that. It's as if he were a spare and understating poet who discovered prose and children's lit all at the same time. I don't know anything about him, and somehow know even less having read his book.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15383002499197046121">This story appears to be some sort of mythic allegory? Or something else. It may yet come to me. Maybe I should give it another star just for giving me something to puzzle about. The writing got smoother along the way as if the author were learning English, and yet Hughes, well, British poet and all that. It's as if he were a spare and understating poet who discovered prose and children's lit all at the same time. I don't know anything about him, and somehow know even less having read his book. The story has inconsistencies and unevenness galore. As I mentioned in the comment section, the art was worse. Are we really ready to celebrate childish art and minimalist story telling with awards and acclaim? Why? What are we saying when we choose one style or story type or book over others? Many things, I suppose.<br />Another odd item: in the back where the publication information is I found these two lines:<br />"Manufactured in China <br />September 2011<br />Random House Children's Books supports the First Amendment and celebrates the right to read."<br />Okaaay...!<br />I really have to dart over to Amazon and read some reviews of this book now. Apparently it's my right.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13041016390136600618">Too many forms of modern illustration just absolutely stink. We're losing imagination and skill with each book of thrown together shapes and disjointe</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13041016390136600618">Too many forms of modern illustration just absolutely stink. We're losing imagination and skill with each book of thrown together shapes and disjointed proportions and Picasso-esque meanderings in color. The art of this edition is not helping the story. The occasional die-cut shape in the middle of the book confuses me as to what age the book is meant for. I suppose the bland story needed to pretend it was interactive, some publishers worry they can't compete with computers. Just give us real art and a rich story, and a book can confidently coexist with computers just fine, thank you.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5128290234153808053"><strong>Ted Hughes a jeho Železný muž</strong><br /><br /><em>Vedeli ste?</em><br />Naša <strong>literárna teória</strong> za?le?uje <strong>literatúru pre deti a mládež</strong> do oblasti takej literárnej tvorby, ktorá zodpovedá vnímaniu vekovo obmedzeného okruhu ?itate?ov spravidla do 14 až 15 roku života. Literárna teória pri tom nekladie dôraz na to, ?i ide o zámernú tvorbu pre deti a mládež, alebo o diela pre dospelých, ktoré sú vhodné i ako ?ítanie pre deti. Za vznik <strong>literatúry pre deti a mládež</strong> je zodpovedná <strong>?udová slovesnos?</strong> podávajúca prostoduchý (?iže detskému ?itate?ovi primeraný) poh?ad na svet. Sú?as?ou literatúry pre deti a mládež sú automaticky aj také diela, ktoré sú svojou významnos?ou, ak ide o vek detského ?itate?a, dvojzna?né – bu? priamo smerujú k porozumeniu a pochopeniu detského príjemcu, alebo ich význam môže vníma? a skôr pochopi? predovšetkým dospelý ?itate?.<br /><br /><strong>Rozprávka</strong> predstavuje jeden zo základných epických žánrov ?udovej slovesnosti a ?itate?ovi sa snaží poda? objektívnu realitu ako nadprirodzenú a s naivnou skuto?nos?ou, t.j. všetko okolo vás je reálne – materiálne. Prostredníctvom tejto svojej fiktívnosti odzrkad?uje ?i už svetonázor pospolitého ?udu, jeho vz?ah ku skuto?nosti, alebo boj za nezávislos? i slobodu.<br /><br /><strong>Rozprávka</strong> údajne vznikla v predhistorickej dobe a traduje sa z generácie na generáciu. Najstaršie rozprávkové pramene siahajú k orientálnej literatúre a jej šírite?mi boli hlavne potulní speváci, ?udoví rozpráva?i, kupci, ale aj remeselníci. Pre rozprávku je charakteristický spôsob jej podania, šírila sa verbálne – ústne, od ktorého závisí nielen výber a charakter postáv, ale aj jej kontrastnos?.<br /><br />V sú?asnosti poznáme <strong>5 základných typov</strong> rozprávok:<br /><br />a) rozprávku fantastickú<br />b) rozprávku démonologickú<br />c) rozprávku zvieraciu (vrátane bájok)<br />d) rozprávku legendovú<br />e) rozprávku realistickú<br /><br />Ke?že <strong>rozprávka, predovšetkým tá ?udová,</strong> prešla od svojho vzniku rôznymi premenami, s jej vývinom úzko súvisí aj vznik autorskej rozprávky. Jej autori na jednej strane aktívne nadväzujú na rôzne tradície a podoby klasickej, ?iže ?udovej rozprávky, ale na druhej strane si ju i zru?ne prispôsobujú. Prispôsobujú ju ?i už dobovým estetickým požiadavkám, alebo na nej stavajú vlastný rozprávkový model.*<br /><br /><br /><strong>Tajomstvo Železného muža</strong><br /><em>Železný muž</em> od <strong>Teda Hughesa</strong> vznikol v roku <strong>1968</strong>. Rôzne mediálne pramene hovoria o tom, že bol napísaný pre autorove deti, ktoré prežívali jedno z najsmutnejších období svojho života. Aby zabudli na smr? blízkeho ?loveka a aby svoj žia? utíšil i sám autor, nielen detského ?itate?a prišiel rozveseli? záhadný Železný muž, ktorý sa z ni?oho ni? objavil priamo v Anglicku.<br /><br /><em>Železný muž</em> sa radí k moderným rozprávkam, ktoré sú svojou formou i výstavbou príbehu ve?mi podobné klasickým rozprávkam fantastickým i realistickým. Napriek tomu, že sa v ?om snúbi hne? nieko?ko špecifických ??t, ktoré sú charakteristické pre detského príjemcu (zmyslovos?, názornos?, hravos?, obraznos? ?i fantastickos? pri vnímaní a poznávaní skuto?nosti), radí sa Železný muž k neintencionálnej vedecko-fantastickej literatúre, ktorej ove?a skôr porozumejú dospelí ?itatelia.<br /><br />Za tento možno pre vä?šinu ?itate?ov zvláštny úkaz môže téma a <strong>dvojdomos?</strong> samotného autora – <strong>Ted Hughes</strong> bol v prvom rade poetom. Jeho básne sa zvä?ša vyzna?ujú temnou, pochmúrnou, apokalyptickou atmosférou. Niekedy sa v nich objaví kúsok mystiky, inokedy decentná dávka cynickosti, sem-tam sú naivne detské a ?isté, inokedy plné farebných metafor a alegórií. Dalo by sa poveda?, že nemajú ?aleko od baladickej tvorby našich klasikov.<br /><br />Tento špecifický autorov rukopis sa, úplne pochopite?ne, premietol aj do jeho tvorby pre deti a mládež. Napriek tomu, že Ted Hughes debutoval vo svete rozprávok v roku 1960 rozprávkovou knihou <em>The Earth Owl and Other Moon People</em>, do povedomia ?itate?skej obce i literárnej kritiky sa zapísal práve svojou útlou (ledva 58-stranovou) detskou knihou The Iron Man (Železný muž).<br /><br />Vä?šina literárnych teoretikov tvrdí, že Železného muža môžete ?íta? dvomi spôsobmi. Bu? ako <strong>modernú vedecko-fantastickú rozprávku</strong>, alebo ako <strong>podobenstvo o vz?ahu medzi ?lovekom, prírodou a technikou</strong> – ako alegóriu o vojnách a vojenských konfliktoch, príbeh o zrade a priate?stve ?i lyrickú polemiku o malosti ?loveka vo vesmíre. Rada by som teraz napísala, že spôsob, akým sa do knihy zahryznete, ovplyvní nejako radikálne vaše ?ítanie. Nie je tomu však tak.<br /><br /><em>Železný muž</em> Teda Hughesa, podobne ako<em>Malý princ</em> Antoina de Saint-Exupéryho ?i <em>anjeli</em> Petra Chudožilova v detskej knihe P?íliš mnoho and?l?, nepotrebuje návod na ?ítanie. Predstavuje kompaktný celok, v ktorom ihne? rozpoznáte autorov odkaz. Ba ?o viac, v istom momente si vás a vaše spomienky dovolí odvia? do študentských ?ias, kedy ste sa snažili odvyknú? si od snovej prí?ažlivosti lyrizovanej prózy, ktorá podobne ako Železný muž Teda Hughesa stavala na nápaditej frekvencii personifikácií, zru?nom alegorizovaní a symbolizovaní vecí a javov. A ktorá rovnako tak prihliadala na domáce spolo?enské okolnosti a reagovala, pomerne citlivo, na napätie medzi sociálnou i prírodnou skuto?nos?ou.<br /><br />Železného muža 28.04.2014 prebralo opä? k životu vydavate?stvo <strong>Albatros</strong>. Napriek tomu, že nieko?ko detských kníh od tohto popredného britského spisovate?a a literárneho laureáta môžete nájs? preložených aj do sloven?iny (a to vrátane Železného muža, postaralo sa o to <strong>Ob?ianske združenie Slnie?kovo</strong>), kvalitou svojho spracovania za ?eskou verziou výrazne zaostávajú. Neve?ká laminovaná detská kniha pre ?itate?ov od 9 rokov vám okrem na oko jednoduchej dejovej línie, v ktorej môžete nájs? návod, ako porozumie? svetu detí ?i dospelých, prinesie 5 strhujúcich fantastických kapitol. Ich ?ítanie vám budú spríjem?ova? hravé ilustrácie <strong>Michala Menšíka</strong>, ktorý sa ukrýva za umeleckým pseudonymom Nikkarin.<br /><br /><strong>Nikkarin</strong> patrí k popredným ?eským komiksovým tvorcom sú?asnej komiksovej generácie. Známy je predovšetkým svojou postapokalyptickou tetralógiou 130, ktorá tematicky ?erpá z prác <strong>Jeana Henriho Gastona Giruada (Moebius) ?i Antoina de Saint-Exupéryho</strong>. Možno práve žáner, ku ktorému sa Nikkarin vo svojich prácach uchy?uje, mal zásluhu na tom, že si ho vydavate?stvo Albatros vybralo za dvorného ilustrátora nad?asového Hughesovho diela.<br /><br />Nech sa pravda ukrýva kdeko?vek, Michalovi Menšíkovi to kreslí, a to ve?mi dobre. Jeho ilustrácie v podobnom duchu, v akom je Železný muž písaný, dop??ajú a obohacujú text o snové výjavy a abstraktné preludy detského sveta v podaní Teda Hughesa, ?ím mu decentne vzdávajú hold. Ich naratívna rovina, síce pomerne ?asto vtla?ená do jedného obrázkového po?a, nielenže drží krok s autorovým rozprávaním, ale aj konkrétnu nosnú pasáž príjemne dynamizuje, ?ím nechá vyniknú? dôležitos? autorovho odkazu, ktorý sa za?al písa? pred dlhými 46 rokmi.<br /><br />Železného muža si teda neob?úbi iba zvedavý chlapec menom Hogarth, a neskôr i celá jeho domácnos?, vrátane obyvate?ov pri?ahlých miest a fariem, ale aj vzrastom ve?ký ?i malý ?itate?. A vek ani v tomto konkrétnom prípade nehrá nijakú dôležitú úlohu. Bez oh?adu na to, ?o máte radi, ?i veríte v duchov alebo drakov, uprednost?ujete iný typ literatúry a rozprávky ?ítate iba sporadicky, nájdete si v tejto útlej knihe kúsok svojho rozprávkového š?astia.<br /><br />A ktovie, možno sa o rok, alebo dva ?i tri, do?káme aj prekladu pokra?ovania Hughesovho železného sveta. The <em>Iron Woman</em> vyšla v roku 1993 a od tohto momentu i ona ?aká na to, kedy ju kone?ne objavíte. Zaho?te teda predsudky, ktoré literatúra pre deti a mládež so sebou v istom veku prináša, a ponorte sa do svojho detstva s príjemnou pomocou rachotiaceho železa, ktoré nerobí ni? iné, len oznamuje príchod Železného muža.<br /><br /><em>Zaujímavos?</em><br />V roku 1968 vyšiel Železný muž i vo vydavate?stve Harper &amp; Row, ktoré ním chcelo spríjemni? ?as milovníkom vedeckej fantastiky a rozprávok v Amerike. Ibaže názov tejto novely bol pomerne ?asto zamie?aný s rovnomenným komiksom spolo?nosti Marvel. Aby sa teda tieto dva tituly neustále nezamie?ali, pozmenilo vydavate?stvo Hughesovej detskej knihe názov. Železný muž sa premenoval na Železného obra (The Iron Gigant), ktorý v roku 1999 inšpiroval filmovú spolo?nos? Warner Brothers k nato?eniu rovnomennej animovanej snímky. <br /><br /><strong>*Použitá literatúra</strong><br />KOPÁL, J. a kol. 1987. Literatúra pre deti a mládež. Bratislava: Slovenské pedagogické nakladate?stvo, 1987, 207 s.<br /><br /><strong>Autor/ka:</strong> Ted Hughes<br /><strong>Názov diela:</strong> Železný muž<br /><strong>Rok vydania:</strong> 2014<br /><strong>Vydavate?stvo:</strong> Albatros media a.s.<br /><strong>Po?et strán:</strong> 58 + 3 strany doslovu<br /><strong>Jazyk:</strong> ?eský<br /><strong>?alší diel:</strong> The Iron Woman<br /><br />Recenzia stránky <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.fantasy-svet.net/?page=recenzia&amp;target_cat=kniha&amp;target_id=751">Fantasy svet</a></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_881849892">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/881849892" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5208457-d-m-dutcher" class="left imgcol" title="D.M. Dutcher "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1338694848p2/5208457.jpg" alt="D.M. Dutcher " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/881849892?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 14, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5208457-d-m-dutcher" class="user" title="D.M. Dutcher ">D.M. Dutcher </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/724659.The_Iron_Giant" title="Paperback 9780375801532" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5208457-d-m-dutcher?shelf=science-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5208457-d-m-dutcher?shelf=children-s" class="actionLinkLite">children-s</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5208457-d-m-dutcher?shelf=gonzo" class="actionLinkLite">gonzo</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer881849892">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2802061922428163844">A very brief book that is nothing like the wonderful movie made from it. Odd, too.<br /><br />The Iron Giant is a mysterious creature with an appetite for metal of all kinds. He quickly lays waste to a farming community until a young boy named Hogarth traps him in a huge pit. Soon the giant is tamed, and just in time too. A huge invader from space has come to take over the earth, and he's our only hope.<br /><br />It's an odd little book. The Giant at first seems to be little more than a walking garbage disposal. There</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2802061922428163844">A very brief book that is nothing like the wonderful movie made from it. Odd, too.<br /><br />The Iron Giant is a mysterious creature with an appetite for metal of all kinds. He quickly lays waste to a farming community until a young boy named Hogarth traps him in a huge pit. Soon the giant is tamed, and just in time too. A huge invader from space has come to take over the earth, and he's our only hope.<br /><br />It's an odd little book. The Giant at first seems to be little more than a walking garbage disposal. There's some environmental subtext considering he eats tractors and fences mostly (engines of things that modify or partition the environment) and that his ultimate "good" use is to eat metal waste. It's all right, but over too fast. <br /><br />However in the second part, he becomes sentient and self-sacrificing in order to fight an absurdly large invader. The space bat-angel-dragon thing is described as being as large as a continent! The Iron Giant beats him in what's essentially a masochism contest, and then the now enslaved "star spirit" sings to the world and sedates/hypnotizes them to peace with the beauty of its music. There's probably some form of national symbolism here, but if so it's confused.<br /><br />It's short, and readable to young kids apart from the random sophisticated word and the dark and odd story. Burying the giant in a pit or the sun burning the space dragon to the point where his riches fall out of him and his physical form is ruined are not a little intense for a young age group. The weird message and symbolism doesn't help either, causing it not to feel coherent.<br /><br />Disappointing compared to the movie, and a mild oddity otherwise. To me it would be comparable to Ursula LeGuin's <a title="Catwings (Catwings, #1) by Ursula K. Le Guin" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13664.Catwings__Catwings___1_">Catwings</a> books, where you get a very brief story with an odd (or even harmful) message.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2802061922428163844">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2660465704706712623">This book has captivated since I was at primary school myself.<br />A young boy called Hogarth discovers a metallic beast, who we come to know is the Iron Man. This 'monster' eats anything it wants, we are witnesses to him eating tractors in half just so he can satisfy his stomach, this book is fully of imagery that relates to children - "with a head as big as a bedroom". I remember it was descriptions like this that had me sat in silence. <br />As the story progresses the Iron Man apparently dies when he f</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2660465704706712623">This book has captivated since I was at primary school myself.<br />A young boy called Hogarth discovers a metallic beast, who we come to know is the Iron Man. This 'monster' eats anything it wants, we are witnesses to him eating tractors in half just so he can satisfy his stomach, this book is fully of imagery that relates to children - "with a head as big as a bedroom". I remember it was descriptions like this that had me sat in silence. <br />As the story progresses the Iron Man apparently dies when he falls off a cliff and breaks into many pieces. End of story you (and I would think) but no the Iron Man returns.<br />The story has the ability to suck in the children's engagement as at one point in the story the adults are on par with the child in the story (Hogarth) when Iron Man returns and no one knows what to do. <br />As the story takes a eventful twist it is then when the true meaning of the story is drawn out. An alien space creature comes to earth to devour everything, however we learn that is has been attracted by all the greed and war on Earth. Hogarth comes to the realisation of the Iron Man's true motives in this great time of need - that he has come to protect Earth from this creature and give them a second chance.<br />This is were the life lesson can be drawn upon, Ted Hughes appears to instilling a sense of peace and harmony within his readers and show that greed and war has serious consequences but that we all have a chance to change. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_216071149">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/216071149" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6215810-max-lawson" class="left imgcol" title="Max Lawson"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1316797098p2/6215810.jpg" alt="Max Lawson" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/216071149?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 27, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6215810-max-lawson" class="user" title="Max Lawson">Max Lawson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/119502.The_Iron_Man" title="Paperback 9780571226122" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer216071149">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1825518140640224715">The Iron Man is a classic childrens novel set over five chapter and designed to be read over five days. The story is about a young boy named Hogarth, who on a fishing trip nearly his town discovers the Iron Man, and the two form a friendship. The local farmers set a trap for the Iron Man as they are sick of the damage this tall-as-a-house giant inflicts on their land, only to find that it fails. Eventually they make peace with the Iron Man, who goes on to save the Earth when a giant bat-creature</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1825518140640224715">The Iron Man is a classic childrens novel set over five chapter and designed to be read over five days. The story is about a young boy named Hogarth, who on a fishing trip nearly his town discovers the Iron Man, and the two form a friendship. The local farmers set a trap for the Iron Man as they are sick of the damage this tall-as-a-house giant inflicts on their land, only to find that it fails. Eventually they make peace with the Iron Man, who goes on to save the Earth when a giant bat-creature threatened to devour every living thing on the planet. Throughout the story it is Hogarth who convinces the adults the good nature of the Iron Man, and who realises that only the giant can save the planet.<br /><br />This story has a wide array of cross-curricular uses in the classroom, most notable for Key Stage Two children. The structure of the story makes it ideal for readers moving onto chapter-based novels, and sequences of reading comprehension, reading with expression, character description and retelling through writing lessons can be built around children progressing through the book. Not limited to literacy, this story can be used to provoke discussion, such as at the beginning when the author asks rhetorical questions like "Where did he come from?". Moreover, the vivid description of the iron man can be adapted to be used to explore the properties of different materials in Science, and the importance of recycling. I have even heard of this book being used in Geography lessons to investigate the kind of debris that can be found on beaches.<br /><br />What stands out most to me however is the vivid character description used throughout the story to describe the way the Iron Man looks, feels and sounds as he moves through the world. This story provides opportunities to significantly widen children's vocabulary and ability to articulate themselves as they consider and come up with their own descriptions of people, places and events.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1825518140640224715">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
